4. [Related Articles](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/41438247045133-Part-1-Preparing-for-Enrollment#h_01KAZW9PSCF1MRPFWJAKCDG33H)

* * *

## **Who This Applies To**

This guide is for **all MMDC students who are preparing to enroll for the upcoming term**—whether you are:

- **A continuing student** who was officially enrolled in the previous term and will proceed with your studies, or
- **A returning student** who took a break, did not enroll in one or more terms, or is currently on an approved **Leave of Absence (LOA)** and plans to resume your studies.

|     |
| --- |
| 📌 **Note:**<br>If you are returning from an LOA or have been inactive for a term or more, please make sure your learner accounts (MMDC Google, email and Camu) are active before enrollment. You may refer to the [**Reactivation of Student Accounts for Returning Students**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/27746288776205) help article for instructions.<br>If you are new to MMDC or transferring from another school, please refer to the appropriate [admission guides found in the MMDC website.](https://www.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/admissions/) |

## **Prepare for Enrollment in 3 Steps**

Preparing for enrollment follows **three simple steps.** These steps help you make informed decisions about your workload, course selection, and financial readiness so you can enter the enrollment period confident and prepared.

### **1\. Determine Your Workload for the Term**

MMDC recognizes that our students come from diverse backgrounds — full-time professionals, working students, and learners balancing other responsibilities. This step empowers you to plan realistically based on what you can handle for the term.

**Ask yourself:**

- **“How many hours per week can I commit to my studies?”**

Each class requires time for three types of learning activities every week:

1. Synchronous class session
2. Mentoring session
3. Independent study or coursework

A 3-unit course generally requires about 1 hour and 15 minutes (1.15 hrs) for each of these activities—usually totaling around 3.5 hours per week per course or subject.

- **Consider your personal, professional, and family commitments.**
- **Aim for a workload that supports both your academic performance and personal well-being.**

You may use and create your own copy of the [Workload Planning Template](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1FViuwviHiUKJWpdOzufrlqOOhNy6rDk1Wsv_DyF_kvQ/copy) to estimate the right number of units for your schedule. Ensure to access the link via your MMDC issued learner Google account.

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41449830920973)[https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1FViuwviHiUKJWpdOzufrlqOOhNy6rDk1Wsv\_DyF\_kvQ/copy](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1FViuwviHiUKJWpdOzufrlqOOhNy6rDk1Wsv_DyF_kvQ/copy)

### **2\. Identify the Courses You Will Enlist In**

Use this step to choose the right courses for the upcoming term based on your **Curriculum Plan (** [**IT**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28639223603469-MMDC-s-Information-Technology-Program) **/** [**BA**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28639222873229-MMDC-s-Business-Administration-Program) **),** your academic standing, and the term’s [course offerings](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/18216038933261). This is also the perfect time to review the **Enrollment Guidelines and Reminders** article to make sure you are selecting courses in the correct sequence and following all pre-requisite, co-requisite, and progression rules. Doing this early helps you avoid enrollment issues, scheduling conflicts, and delays in your academic timeline.

#### **A. Start with your Curriculum Plan (** [**IT**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28639223603469-MMDC-s-Information-Technology-Program) **/** [**BA**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28639222873229-MMDC-s-Business-Administration-Program) **)**

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41450349680525)**Curriculum Plan (** [**IT**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28639223603469-MMDC-s-Information-Technology-Program) **/** [**BA**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28639222873229-MMDC-s-Business-Administration-Program) **)**

Your Curriculum Plan outlines the recommended sequence of courses per term. These subjects are arranged like building blocks—each course builds on the knowledge and skills developed in the earlier ones. The sequence is organized according to what is recommended for **Year 1-Term 1**, **Year 1-Term 2** and so on, guiding you through a structured progression from foundational subjects to more advanced or specialized courses.

Because the curriculum follows this structured progression, some courses have pre-requisites or co-requisites to help guide your learning path and prevent gaps in understanding.

|     |
| --- |
| **📌** **Definitions:**<br>- **Pre-requisite**– a required course you must complete and pass before enrolling in a more advanced subject.<br>- **Co-requisite** – a paired course that must be taken in the same term because the concepts support each other (e.g., Lecture + Laboratory). |

|     |
| --- |
| **📌** **Understanding Your Student Status**<br>As you review your **Curriculum Plan (** [**IT**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28639223603469-MMDC-s-Information-Technology-Program) **/** [**BA**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28639222873229-MMDC-s-Business-Administration-Program) **)**, it also helps to understand whether you are a regular or irregular student, as this affects how closely you can follow the recommended sequence.<br>- **Regular students** are those who have no failed subjects and are currently on track with their Curriculum Plan. They can typically follow the intended progression (Year 1–Term 1 courses, Year 1–Term 2 courses, and so on) without interruptions. <br>- **Irregular students** are those who have failed grades or academic deficiencies that may prevent them from taking certain courses on time—especially those with prerequisites. When this happens, your term to term Plan of Study may need to be adjusted or restructured. <br>In these cases, the student may still refer to the Curriculum Plan but will have to consider courses that needs to be re-taken. If further assistance is needed, you may raise a ticket [here](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/requests/new) to consult with the Integrated Advisors or you may also request for an Academic Advising session with the Program Heads. <br>Understanding your status helps you anticipate whether you can follow the standard sequence or whether you may need additional planning and support for the term. |

#### **B. Check your grades via the Camu portal:**

- A course with a Fail (F) must be re-taken and passed.
- A course with an Incomplete (INC) should NOT be enlisted again. INCs follow a different process. No re-enrollment is needed to complete the course. Refer to the [Course Completion Guide](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/32265959292557) for next steps.

#### **C. If you have prior college credits, review your Request for Credit Evaluation Form to confirm which courses were credited.**

- **Credited courses do not need to be enrolled.**

|     |
| --- |
| **📌****Important:**<br>If you choose to (or by accident) enroll in a course that has already been credited, this means you are voluntarily overriding the credited result. Once you enroll in that course, the credit is no longer honored, and the subject will now be treated as a regular enrolled course that you must complete and pass. This decision cannot be reversed, and the course will remain part of your academic record for that term. |

#### **D. Check the** [**Course Offerings**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/18216038933261) **for the upcoming term**

- Look at available schedules, sections, and faculty assignments (if available).
- Note any conflicts or overlaps.
- You can now proceed with preparing a shortlist of courses or a Per [Term Enrollment Plan](https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1M1fSb4NMia6ZFsKa8YhP9lfzbygigsZQ/copy) that balance your schedule, your work, family commitments, academic goals and your expected graduation timeline.

### **3\. Financial & Administrative Check-Up**

Before enrollment starts, ensure that all financial and administrative requirements are in order.

#### **A. Confirm your student account standing**

- Clear any remaining balances from previous terms (tuition or other fees).
- Ensure device payments (if applicable) are up to date.
- Outstanding obligations must be settled before you can re-enroll.

#### **B. Review payment scheme options**

- **Choose between:**  - **Full payment, or**
  - **Installment plan (initial payment + monthly installments).**

Your initial payment must meet the required minimum (e.g., 20% of the current term’s tuition) to be officially counted as enrolled.

#### **C. Check for applicable discounts**

- You may be eligible for certain financial benefits, such as the **Miscellaneous Fees Discount** (a 40% reduction for students enrolled in 9 units or less) or the [**Asenso Discount**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/37450066753805-Asenso-Scholarship-Discount-Program) (an additional 16% for students admitted from SY 2023 onwards).
- Please note that the +16% Asenso Discount is **not automatically applied**—you will need to submit an application each term to avail of them.

* * *

### **❓ FAQs — Enrollment Preparations**

|     |
| --- |
| **1\. How do I know which courses to take first?** |
| Start with your Curriculum Plan. Courses are arranged in recommended order. Follow all pre-requisites and co-requisites. |
| **2\. How many units should I take if I have a full-time job?** |
| Students with full-time work and with less than 10 hours availability per week are recommended to enroll in 6–9 units to maintain balance and avoid burnout. |
| **3\. What should I do if I received an INC last term?** |
| You should not re-enroll in a course marked INC. Instead, file a [Request to Complete Course](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/32265959292557-Course-Completion-for-INC-Grades) via IA Services. |
| **4\. What if I’m unsure how to prepare my schedule?** |
| You may request help from your Integrated Advising Team. They can help you interpret your Curriculum Plan, estimate workload, and sequence your courses properly. |
| **5\. What tools do I need before enrollment starts?** |
| - Your Curriculum Plan<br>- Course Offerings for the term<br>- Academic Calendar<br>- Your weekly availability<br>- List of previously passed/failed/incomplete subjects |

* * *

- [Course Offerings (Per Term)](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/related/click?data=BAh7CjobZGVzdGluYXRpb25fYXJ0aWNsZV9pZGwrCA2jh0CREDoYcmVmZXJyZXJfYXJ0aWNsZV9pZGwrCA3I%2FhewJToLbG9jYWxlSSIKZW4tdXMGOgZFVDoIdXJsSSJAL2hjL2VuLXVzL2FydGljbGVzLzE4MjE2MDM4OTMzMjYxLUNvdXJzZS1PZmZlcmluZ3MtUGVyLVRlcm0GOwhUOglyYW5raQk%3D--f4cec5d135f7d393fd61e1f5eaad112b5547a60b)

## Part 3: MMDC's Online Enrollment Steps – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/41439855591437-Part-3-MMDC-s-Online-Enrollment-Steps

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/41439855591437-Part-3-MMDC-s-Online-Enrollment-Steps#main-content)

This guide provides a detailed step-by-step process for enrollment, covering course enlistment, finalization, and payment. Before proceeding, ensure you have identified the courses you need to enroll in by referring to [**Part 1: Preparing for Enrollment**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/41438247045133) **and** [**Part 2: Enrollment Guidelines & Policies**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/41439901133965).

### **How to Enroll: A Step-by-step Guide**

**STEP 1:**

Log-in to your **Camu Student Portal.**

- Open a web browser and navigate to [https://www.mycamu.com/](https://www.mycamu.com/)
- Log in by keying in your credentials (username and password) or log in via Google SSO.

**STEP 2:**

Access the **Semester Enrollment Menu.**

- Once logged in, locate and click the **Enrollment** tab from the left menu column of your home page.

![Screen Shot 2024-03-25 at 10.50.56 AM.png](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439855576461)

- Select **Semester Enrollment.** This will direct you to Camu's Semester Enrollment page.

![Screen Shot 2024-03-25 at 10.53.15 AM.png](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439886232589)

- Choose the upcoming term/ semester you intend to enroll in.

![Screen](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439855582477)

- Once you click on the Term, the courses offered for the term will be displayed below.

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439855583245)

- Choose **Full Registration**. Please note that only courses enrolled under the **Full Registration** menu will be officially registered.
  - **Note:** Make sure you are viewing the **FULL REGISTRATION** list of courses. MMDC currently only offers Full Registration type of courses. **If you have an INC grade from a previous term, you do not need to re-enroll these courses.**Instead, you need to apply for a course completion request via the IA Services.

  - ![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439886234381)

**STEP 3:**

Enlist in your chosen course and preferred section and schedule.

- Under Full Registration, the courses offered for the term will be displayed.
- Review the available courses, section and schedule. Click the **Enroll** button to enlist in your chosen courses. Separately, _you may also view the list of Course Offerings for the term here:_ [_**Course Offerings**_](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/18216038933261-Course-Offerings-Per-Term) [_._](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/18216038933261-Course-Offerings-SY-2023-24)

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439855584269)

Note that the blue portion is just a header; it displays the Course Code and its number of units, and the enrollment type. Again, ensure that it says Full Registration.

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439886237837)

The course, section, and schedule available are below the header **in a white background.**

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439855585677)

Each course or subject has the following information:

- Section
- GE/ IT or BA
- Mentor
- Date (indicates the start and end date of the term)
- Days and Times
- The status will indicate the number of enrollees so far.

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439886241165)

- Repeat this step until you've enrolled in all the courses you intend to enroll in for the current term.

**STEP 4:**

Do a **final review** of the courses you enrolled in. **Finalize your Enrollment** and provide your preferred **Payment Scheme** via the [**Enrollment Finalization GForm**](https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSeB6VRoAhmZwHrC3Q1Is6kjKSLvKBrzg53zHnC4amEKyDoRAA/viewform) **.** As part of our updated process, you can submit the Enrollment Finalization Form **only once**. Please review your preferred payment scheme carefully before submitting, as **no revisions will be allowed afterward**.

- Do a final review of the courses you enlisted in.

1. To know the number of units you've already enrolled, you may refer to this.

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439855587725)

2\. Toggle on **All**, **Enrolled**, **Not Enrolled** to filter the list.

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439886242701)

3\. To change and remove a course you've enlisted in, navigate and click the **Drop button** across the section you prefer.

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439855588621)

- When you are ready with your selected courses, submit an Enrollment Finalization Request via the [Enrollment Finalization GForm](https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSeB6VRoAhmZwHrC3Q1Is6kjKSLvKBrzg53zHnC4amEKyDoRAA/viewform).

![Screenshot 2026-03-11 at 11.27.54 AM.png](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/44188117927565)

**STEP 5:**

Await your **Generated Statement of Account (GSA)** to be posted in Camu's Billing Menu during the GSA posting period.

- After finalizing your enrollment, wait for your GSA (Generated Statement of Account) to be posted.

You may view your GSA on the Billing tab of your Camu account.

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41439855589517)

While waiting, you may use the available calculator on the [Help Center](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/17463924733453-Tuition-Fee-Calculator) page to get an estimate of your total fees and prepare accordingly.

**STEP 6:**

Submit your **proof of payment** by uploading it via the [**Proof of Payment GForm**](https://forms.gle/3SgeRadiVj4Lzauq7) **.**

**STEP 7:**

**Enrollment Confirmation.**

- Once your payment is verified, you will receive an enrollment confirmation email, indicating that you are officially enrolled for the term.

This is the last and final step of the enrollment process.

**Helpful Links:**

- [**Enrollment Guide for Continuing Students**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/35510449781517-Enrollment-Guide-for-Continuing-Students)
- [**Course Offerings**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/18216038933261-Course-Offerings-SY-2023-24)
- [**Proof of Payment GForm**](https://forms.gle/3SgeRadiVj4Lzauq7)
- [**Enrollment Finalization GForm**](https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSeB6VRoAhmZwHrC3Q1Is6kjKSLvKBrzg53zHnC4amEKyDoRAA/viewform)

## Part 2: Enrollment Guidelines & Policies – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/41439901133965-Part-2-Enrollment-Guidelines-Policies

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/41439901133965-Part-2-Enrollment-Guidelines-Policies#main-content)

## **Overview**

Understanding MMDC’s enrollment rules and course selection principles is essential to making informed decisions each term. This article outlines the key policies that guide enrollment — including course sequencing, prerequisites, co-requisites, unit loads, academic standing considerations, and common enrollment issues to avoid. These guidelines will help you make choices that keep you aligned with your **Curriculum Plan (** [**IT**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28639223603469-MMDC-s-Information-Technology-Program) **/** [**BA**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28639222873229-MMDC-s-Business-Administration-Program) **)** and your projected graduation timeline.

This article works **hand-in-hand with** [**Part 1: Preparing for Enrollment,**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/41438247045133) which helps you review your academic standing and plan your course list before the enrollment period begins. Once you’re ready to proceed, you may follow [**Part 3: MMDC's Online Enrollment Steps**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/41439855591437) for detailed instructions on completing your online enrollment in the system.

## **Enrollment Standards & Course Policies**

### **Follow Your Cohort’s Curriculum Plan**

- Enroll in courses aligned with your cohort’s Curriculum Plan—this ensures the right sequence and avoids delays.
- Refer to the Curriculum Plan of the SY when you were admitted to MMDC. If your first year was SY2023-2024, you will follow this Curriculum Plan up until your graduation.
- Maximum units per term are set in the Curriculum. Do not exceed that unless you seek overload approval through a separate process. Refer to the article: [How to Request for Study Overload](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/32574438451853).

### **Pre-requisite & Co-requisite Requirements**

- **Pre-requisites:** These are courses you must complete **before** enrolling in advanced courses.  - If you have an INC (Incomplete) in a prerequisite, you cannot take its advanced course until the pre-requisite course is passed.
- **Co-requisites:** These are courses meant to be taken **together in the same term** (e.g., Lecture + Lab courses).  - Ensure you enroll in both parts in the same section/term.

Following the correct course sequence ensures you have the foundation needed for more advanced concepts and skills. Enrolling out of sequence can lead to difficulties, gaps in understanding, and may increase your chances of falling behind. In many cases, students who take advanced courses too early end up filing a **Dropping Request (DRP)** once the workload becomes overwhelming. **A DRP will appear on your transcript of records and will not qualify for any tuition fee adjustment or deduction.**

### **Special Grades and Re-enrollment**

1. ##### Courses marked **INC (Incomplete)** or **C (Continuing)** should not be re-enrolled. Instead, you must file a [Request to Complete Course](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/32265959292557) within the allowed period stated in the [Calendar of Activities](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28318507978637-MMDC-s-Calendar-of-Activities). If the request is not filed within the completion window, the grade will lapse and be rendered as 5.00 (Fail)


|     |
| --- |
| 📌 **Definitions**<br>- **INC (Incomplete)**– This applies to regular courses when you have not submitted all the required coursework within the term. You must complete the remaining requirement through the Request to Complete process within the period in the succeeding term.<br>- **C (Continuing)** – This applies to integrative courses such as Feasibility/Capstone or Practicum. These courses have a longer completion period, usually spanning one to two succeeding terms. Once you finish the remaining requirements, file the Request to Complete during the term you complete the course. |

2. **Dropped Courses (DRP)** are considered as not passed, the course must be re-enrolled in a future term as required in your curriculum.

3. **Failed Courses (5.00)****\-** Any course with a failing grade must also be re-enrolled and passed before you can proceed with any advanced subjects that depend on it.

4. **Credited Courses**are courses that have been formally credited and do not need to be enrolled. However, if you choose to enroll in a credited course, you are voluntarily overriding the credit, and the course will now need to be completed and passed. This decision cannot be reversed.

### **Courses for Special Consideration**

1. **Capstone, Thesis, and Feasibility Study**

These are culminating courses in your program and require strong preparation.



| **For BSIT Students: Capstone 1 & 2** | **For BSBA Students: Feasibility Study / Thesis** |
| --- | --- |
| Capstone courses synthesize everything you’ve learned. While Capstone 1 has no formal prerequisites, it is strongly recommended that you complete the following foundational areas first:<br>   - Computing Fundamentals<br>   - Programming (e.g., MO-IT103, MO-IT110)<br>   - Data Management<br>   - Computer Networks<br>   - System Analysis and Design<br>_These courses give you the essential skills needed to plan, execute, and deliver a strong Capstone project._ | If you plan to enroll in MO-MKT2002 Thesis or Feasibility Study, ensure that:<br>   - You have completed all your major courses in your specialization<br>   - You are prepared to dedicate sufficient time, as these are labor-intensive culminating requirements |

2. **Equivalent (Parallel) Courses**

As the curriculum plans evolve from school year to school year, it at times result to varying versions of previous courses that cover the same essential content, but with revised titles, codes, or components. In MMDC’s curriculum, some older courses now have newer equivalents:

- MO-IT161 (LEC & LAB) → previously MO-IT120
- MO-IT162 (LEC & LAB) → previously MO-IT125
- MO-IT163 (LEC & LAB) → previously MO-IT139

If you have already passed the first course, you should not anymore enroll in its equivalent version, as it covers the same competencies and will not be rendered as additional credit.

In this specific scenario, the only difference between the first and the second version is the laboratory component.

**As a general rule, always refer and follow your cohort’s Curriculum Plan.**

3. **College Logic and Math & Language and Communications**

If you **Passed** PPC Assessment as part of the admissions process, you **should not** re-enroll in the remediation courses **MO-MATH034 (College Logic and Math)** and **MO-ENG039 (Language and Communication)**. These subjects are considered as **credited**, and you are no longer required to take them.

|     |
| --- |
| 📌 **Important:**<br>If you choose to enroll in these courses, this means you are intentionally **retaking** them. Doing so will **forfeit the credited result**, and the course will now need to be completed and passed as a regular enrolled subject. This decision **cannot be reversed**. |

### **Final Recommendations**

As you finalize your enrollment, make sure to follow the dates indicated in the [**Academic Calendar**,](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/sections/28318507978637-MMDC-s-Calendar-of-Activities) including enlistment periods, payment deadlines, and the Course Load Revision window. If you need help choosing your courses or clarifying your academic path, feel free to consult your **Integrated Advisor**, **Program Head**, or **Mentor**—they are here to guide you. Keep copies of your academic plan, payment confirmations, and any forms you submit so you can track your progress confidently. Planning your schedule carefully helps you stay on track and avoid delays in your graduation timeline.

## Introducing the Professor + IT Coach Model: An Improved BSIT Learning Experience – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/41965197681293-Introducing-the-Professor-IT-Coach-Model-An-Improved-BSIT-Learning-Experience

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/41965197681293-Introducing-the-Professor-IT-Coach-Model-An-Improved-BSIT-Learning-Experience#main-content)

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41965568886541)

**Hello MMDC Learners,**

At MMDC, we’re committed to giving you the support you need to thrive as digital students, even while working. Each term, we look at your performance, listen to your feedback, and identify opportunities to make your learning experience smoother, clearer, and more responsive.

Over the past terms, many of you shared what helps you learn best:

- faster and clearer feedback,
- more time and guidance from your Professors,
- consistent standards across sections, and
- support that keeps up with your busy schedules.

We hear you — and we’re excited to introduce an improvement designed to make your BSIT experience even stronger.

* * *

Starting this coming term **(T2-SY2526)**, the **BSIT program** will begin using the **Professor + IT Coach (ITC) Model,** an enhanced learning support structure that brings faster feedback, more guidance, and a more consistent academic experience.

## What is an IT Coach?

An **IT Coach (ITC)** is an industry practitioner who has been trained in MMDC’s standards, rubrics, and coaching approach.

Their role is to:

- check and assess your outputs,
- give clear, actionable, rubric-based feedback,
- support your progress throughout the term, and
- help ensure your learning stays on track.

They work closely with your Professor and Program Head to maintain aligned academic expectations.

## How does the new model work?

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41965568886925)

Your **Professor** continues to lead your learning for the course. This includes:

- facilitating all synchronous sessions,
- guiding your overall mastery of course outcomes,
- providing academic mentorship,
- addressing complex questions, and
- supervising and calibrating the IT Coaches.

Your **IT Coach** works alongside your Professor and supports the same learners/cohort throughout the term. They provide timely assessments, clear feedback, and continuity of support.

Together, your **Professor + ITC** form your learning team — giving you more people, more guidance, and more consistent support.

This model allows each role to focus on what they do best: **Professors** on teaching, **IT Coaches** on providing timely, reliable, rubric-based feedback.

## What Better Experiences Can You Expect?

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/41965568887181)

1. **More Focused Support From Professor:**Because Professors are supported by ITCs, they can dedicate more time to the parts of learning that matter most to you:   - Deeper guidance
   - More meaningful mentoring
   - Clearer explanations during sync sessions
   - Plenary support for complex project questions
2. **Faster, Clearer Feedback:** ITCs help review your outputs using calibrated rubrics, so you can expect:   - Quicker, more consistent turnaround times
   - Feedback you can immediately apply
   - More predictable progress checks
3. **Stronger, More Consistent Support:** Instead of relying on just one person, you gain a team supporting your learning. This ensures your experience remains strong even as the BSIT program grows.
4. **A Better Experience for Working Students:** This model is designed with your schedules and responsibilities in mind. **The goal is simple: less waiting, clearer guidance, more steady support, and more time focused on learning.**

* * *

## Frequently Asked Questions (FAQs)

|     |
| --- |
| **Will I still have my Professor?** |
| Yes. Absolutely. Your Professor remains your main mentor, guide, and academic lead. |
| **What exactly does an IT Coach do?** |
| IT Coaches check outputs, provide rubric-based feedback, and help ensure your learning progress is supported. They are trained to apply consistent standards across sections. |
| **Does this mean my class size is getting bigger?** |
| Expect your synch sessions to have more people, which may help with several activities relying on sharing experiences, partnerships, or other interactive events. Professors will oversee more learners - but you are actually gaining more focused and personalized support now that IT Coaches are part of your learning team. |
| **Who gives my grades?** |
| ITCs assess your outputs based on MMDC’s rubrics. They’re trained to give consistent, transparent feedback. Professors oversee the academic standards and ensure alignment across the course. |
| **Will the way I submit outputs or attend classes change?** |
| No changes on your end. Your workflow stays the same. You’ll just start experiencing clearer feedback, quicker turnaround times, and more accessible guidance |
| **How qualified are the IT Coaches?** |
| ITCs are industry practitioners who have been carefully selected based on their ability to understand and support MMDC’s learning model. They bring current industry experience to ensure they help prepare you for the real-world. |
| **Why is MMDC implementing this now?** |
| Your feedback helps shape how we improve the BSIT program. Many of you shared that timely guidance, consistent standards, and clearer feedback make a big difference — so this model is our way of strengthening the support you receive. |

* * *

## Your Student ID at MMDC – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/42062920332685-Your-Student-ID-at-MMDC

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/42062920332685-Your-Student-ID-at-MMDC#main-content)

## **Overview**

MMDC issues **digital student IDs** as part of our onboarding process. This article explains when and how IDs are released, what to do if there are issues with your ID details, and what to expect regarding physical IDs and lanyards.

* * *

## **What is the process for requesting student IDs?**

Student IDs are **sent within the first month after the official start of the term**.

- IDs are issued based on the information submitted during admissions.
- If additional or updated information is required, the team will proactively reach out to you.
- If you were contacted due to **incomplete ID data**, or if you **received your ID with discrepancies**, you may request ID issuance through this form:

[**ID Request Form**](https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSe2ZarKx5YdKdaL-G1S7LFN-J85u5sMfD_pttb-zkmFAoNonQ/viewform)

* * *

## **Does MMDC issue physical IDs?**

No. As a **digital-first institution**, MMDC issues **digital IDs only**.

- Students may **print their digital IDs at their own expense** if needed.
- **MMDC does not provide printed or laminated IDs.**

* * *

## **Where can I purchase an MMDC lanyard?**

MMDC currently **does not sell lanyards or official merchandise**.

- However, students are encouraged to join MMDC activities, where **official merch items (including lanyards)** are occasionally raffled or given away.

* * *

If you have concerns about your ID status or details, [submit a request](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/requests/new) through the [Help Center](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us) for assistance.

* * *

## What Happens If I Fail the Coursera Integrity Check? – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/42031620536461-What-Happens-If-I-Fail-the-Coursera-Integrity-Check

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/42031620536461-What-Happens-If-I-Fail-the-Coursera-Integrity-Check#main-content)

## **Overview**

This article explains what happens if your Coursera submission fails an Integrity Check and outlines your responsibilities as a learner.

* * *

If you fail the **Coursera Integrity Check**, **you are responsible for reaching out to your mentor** to address the issue promptly. A failed integrity check does **not automatically result in disciplinary action**, but it does require immediate attention.

* * *

### **What You Need to Do**

1. **Contact your mentor as soon as possible** after receiving the Integrity Check notification.
2. Be prepared to **explain your submission** and provide context on how the work was completed.
3. Cooperate fully during the review process.

* * *

### **What Happens After Review**

After discussing the case, your mentor may:

- Allow a **resubmission**, or
- Request a **revision** of the work

The outcome depends on the mentor’s assessment of the submission and supporting explanation.

* * *

### **Important Reminders**

- You are expected to submit **original work** at all times.
- Integrity checks are part of MMDC’s commitment to **academic standards**.
- Failure to proactively communicate with your mentor may **delay resolution**.


For a full explanation of expectations and violations, please review the **Academic Integrity** article:

👉 [_Academic Integrity Policy and Guidelines_](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/32744004272781-Academic-Integrity)

* * *

If you need further assistance, you may also [**submit a support ticket**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/requests/new) through the [Help Center](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us).

* * *

## External Financial Aid and Loan Options – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/42659701652365-External-Financial-Aid-and-Loan-Options

4. [HCQWARTA by Home Credit Philippines](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/42659701652365-External-Financial-Aid-and-Loan-Options#h_01KEXSQANRJD8Q2EY87P3DT466)

## OWWA Scholarship

Overseas Workers Welfare Administration (OWWA) Education for Development Scholarship Program (EDSP) a scholarship grant to qualified dependents of OFWs consisting of a maximum of Php60,000.00 per school year until the completion of a baccalaureate course (4-5 years). For incoming freshmen, the selection of scholars is determined through the DOST national examinations. Only the top 1,000 qualifiers are considered for entry as freshmen; 600 slots are for those in 2nd to 5th year college level who are enrolled in any Philippine-based college or university.

**General Qualifications**

1\. Must be a child of an active OWWA member; or Sibling of a single or married but childless active OWWA member

2\. Must have NO AVAILMENT of any OWWA Scholarship Program by other Members of the OFW Family

**EDSP CATEGORY 1 (Incoming 1st Year College)**

- Must be single
- Must not be more than 21 years old
- Must be Grade 12 graduating student
- Must have a GWA of 80% or its equivalent

**EDSP CATEGORY 2 (2nd to 5th Year College)**

- Must be single
- Must not be more than 30 years old
- Must have a GWA of at least 85% or its equivalent
- Must have no failing grades
- Must be enrolled in a Philippine-based college/university

**Requirements:**

The basic requirements to be submitted by the applicants upon application online are the following:

**1\. Proof of Identity**

1.1 OFW - Copy of Valid OFW Passport Bio or Info Page

1.2 Dependent

1.2.1 Valid School I.D. or any available Valid I.D.

1.2.2 Birth Certificate or Baptismal

**2\. Proof of grades from the previous School Year**

(i.e. Form 137 or Form 10 \[TOR\], Form 138 or Report Card, or Certificate of Grades from the School)

**3\. 2x2 I.D. Picture of the OFW's Dependent (Child or Sibling Applicant)**

White background

With name tag and signature of applicant

**Note:** For those students who cannot present the current or previous semester grades, the grades within the last two (2) school years can be considered as reference

**Important Notes for Online Application**

- Use a valid and working e-mail address.
- Provide a working mobile number to be able to contact you if there is a need to, refer to the application.
- Do not make multiple applications as may this affect the process of verification/evaluation of your applications.
- Make sure to prepare ALL REQUIRED documents/requirements/information/data about the scholarship applicant and the OFW before making the online application. This will serve as a basis for the first come, first serve policy of processing the application.
- When filling out the required information, please ensure that the names and words are spelled correctly and completely.
- Be sure to have a stable and strong internet connection.

Visit this link to learn more: [https://scholarship.owwa.gov.ph/](https://scholarship.owwa.gov.ph/)

## PVAO (Philippine Veterans Affairs Office) Scholarship

THE PVAO Educational Benefit Program is part of the package of benefits being administered by the Philippine Veterans Affairs Office which entitles a veteran (WWII, Korean War and Vietnam War), or his qualified beneficiary, to study at any school, college, university or institution recognized by the Commission on Higher Education (CHED). The benefit covers payment of tuition, matriculation, registration, clinical, affiliation, military training, diploma and graduation fees.

**Eligibility:**

a) Veterans of WWII, PEFTOK, and PHILCAG Veterans

b) Surviving spouse (in case the veteran/surviving spouse did not apply for the benefit or if the benefit was applied for but has not been used or has been partially used.)

**Nature of Benefit**

1\. Payment of school fees- Maximum of P60,000 /Academic Year

2\. One time payment of Review Fee amounting to P18,000

**Requirements for Filing an Application**

1\. Military Service Record of Veteran issued by the Office of the Adjutant General (OTAG), AFP/ Certification issued by PVAO or the Military Service Board (MSB), if veteran is a “Deserving Guerilla”;

2\. Certificate of Marriage of veteran and his spouse issued by PSA;

3\. Death certificate of veteran issued by PSA (If deceased);

4\. Death certificate of surviving spouse of veteran issued by PSA (If deceased);

5\. Waiver of Rights of all the children of veteran in favor of the proposed beneficiary;

6\. Birth certificate of beneficiary’s parent issued by PSA (Child of the veteran); and

7\. Marriage certificate of beneficiary’s parents issued by PSA.

Requirements for Change of School/ Course

1\. Course curriculum program

2\. Latest Registration form

3\. Transcript of record from the previous school

4\. Photocopy of AWARD (copy for student)

5\. Scholarship Credit Card (Blue Book)

REPLACEMENT OF SCHOLARSHIP CREDIT CARD

1\. Affidavit of loss

2\. Copy of AWARD (copy for student)

REQUIREMENTS FOR INITIAL PAYMENT OF SCHOOL BILLS

1\. Duly Accomplished Copy of AWARD (marked “Billing”),

2\. Duly accomplished School Enrolment Confirmation Slip (Below Notice of Approval)

3\. Notarized Contract

4\. Personal Information Sheet

5\. Finger Printing Form

6\. Duly Accomplished Certificate of Enrolment form/ Latest School Registration Form with Assessment of Fees;

7\. Official Email Addresses of School Registrar & Accounting Office (preferably the edu.ph email address)

8\. Bank Account details of School (for payment of school bill)

REQUIREMENTS FOR SUCCEEDING SCHOOL BILLS

1\. Duly Accomplished Certificate of Enrolment form/Latest School Registration Form with Assessment of Fees

2\. Original or Certified COPY OF GRADES from previous school term (All grades PASSED)

REQUIREMENTS FOR REIMBURSEMENT OF SCHOOL BILLS

1\. Letter Request for Reimbursement

2\. Duly Accomplished Certificate of Enrolment form/ Latest School Registration Form with Assessment of Fees

3\. Original or Certified Copy of Grades from previous school term (All grades PASSED)

4\. Bank Account Details of Student (for depositing of reimbursement check)

COVERAGE OF THE P60,000 ANNUAL ENTITLEMENT

School fees authorized by the CHED and appearing in the prospectus, catalog, or brochure of the school. It does not cover allowances (book, uniform, etc.)

LIMITATIONS OF THE SCHOLARSHIP

Scholars are entitled to receive subsidy/support for one (1) basic course (undergraduate, graduate, postgraduate) except in cases where scholarship has been previously awarded to and partially used by the veteran, surviving spouse, or any of his direct descendants. The subsequent grantee shall only be entitled to the remaining period of entitlement.

For further concerns or inquiries, please contact:

MS. MA. MAGGIE GRACE B. SAHAGUN-SALVA

Email: [educationalbenefit.customercare@pvao.gov.ph](mailto:educationalbenefit.customercare@pvao.gov.ph)

Telephone: (02) 8352-8510

Mobile Number: 0929-660-2313

EB Official FB Page: [https://www.facebook.com/pvaoiskolarngbayani](https://www.facebook.com/pvaoiskolarngbayani)

## GrabScholar College Scholarships

Supported by the GrabForGood Fund, GrabScholar is an educational assistance program aimed at facilitating economic empowerment to uplift the welfare of the community at large. Grab empowers underprivileged students and jobseekers with scholarships and bursaries so they can have access to education, additional training, and job opportunities.

This educational assistance program is open to incoming first-year college students enrolling in the following programs or degrees: Business, STEM (except medical courses), and Sustainability-related courses. Selected applicants will receive full coverage of tuition and miscellaneous fees, assistance for school supplies, and a monthly allowance.

For inquiries, you may send an email to [grabscholarcollegescholarship@gmail.com](mailto:grabscholarcollegescholarship@gmail.com)

## HCQWARTA by Home Credit Philippines

HCQWARTA is a virtual credit line of Home Credit that you can use to buy load, pay bills, pay for your groceries by generating a barcode, top-up your Lazada wallet, and buy discounted vouchers.

You can receive a Home Credit HCQWARTA offer if you have an active account with Home Credit and are eligible for the HCQWARTA offer.

To use HCQWARTA to pay your bills:

1. Open your Home Credit app and tap “Pay Bills.”
2. Choose Biller → Education → search for MAPUA MALAYAN DIGITAL COLLEGE (MMDC).
3. Provide your account details.
4. Review your payment details and choose Home Credit Qwarta as your payment option. Then tap “Confirm Payment,” enter your PIN, and you’re done!

You may also watch this link: [https://youtu.be/6HsByFQY-\_k?si=671N3IVUvUjhgGcn](https://youtu.be/6HsByFQY-_k?si=671N3IVUvUjhgGcn)

## Google Meet Troubleshooting Guide – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43066343347981-Google-Meet-Troubleshooting-Guide

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43066343347981-Google-Meet-Troubleshooting-Guide#main-content)

|     |
| --- |
| ## **Overview**<br>This article helps you troubleshoot common **Google Meet technical issues** you might encounter during MMDC online classes and meetings. It includes steps to resolve audio, video, connectivity, and login problems so you can stay connected without interruption. Use this guide when your camera, microphone, or screen sharing isn’t working as expected. |

* * *

## **Table of Contents**

- [Meeting Code does not work](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/17595961894541-Meeting-code-does-not-work)
- [Camera and Microphone were denied access](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/17596743309069-Camera-and-microphone-were-denied-access)
- [Poor video quality during meeting](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/17596778563853-Poor-video-quality-during-meeting)


* * *

## [**Meeting Code does not Work**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43066343347981-Google-Meet-Troubleshooting-Guide\#h_01KG4NCJQX36R287VTF3TB53N3)

**BACKGROUND**

_Meeting codes are given by the organizer to provide access to meeting rooms in Google Meet. If a meeting code does not work, it means that the code does not exist and Google Meet is not able to recognize it._

### What do I do if the meeting code does not work?

Kindly follow these troubleshooting steps if you encounter issues with your Google Meeting code:

1. Check if you have the correct code.

2. If you have an email invite, [join via email](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/17567548588301-Join-a-Meeting-via-Email) or check the code in the **Meeting Link**of the email invite.


**NOTE**: The meeting code is the string of letters at the end of the meeting link without the hyphens.

3. Contact the meeting organizer if the code still doesn't work.


[> > \> back to top](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43066343347981-Google-Meet-Troubleshooting-Guide#h_01KG4J2YWK6721SAE1B9YMGDX7)

* * *

## [**Camera and Microphone were Denied Access**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43066343347981-Google-Meet-Troubleshooting-Guide\#h_01KG4PN2W09H66D7AGYP55Y92N)

**BACKGROUND**

_Applications are designed to get the permission of the users to grant access to the device's camera and microphone. In the first use of Google Meet, the application will ask for your permission to access your device's camera and microphone. If you are not able to grant permission, your camera and microphone will not work properly during meetings._

### What do I do if my camera and microphone were denied access?

Kindly follow these troubleshooting steps if you encounter issues with your camera and/or microphone access:

**Step 1**

Open a Google Chrome browser or a new tab.

![1-cam.jpg](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43066405529869)

**Step 2**

Go to [Google Meet](http://meet.google.com/).

![2-cam.jpg](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43066405533069)

**Step 3**

Click **New Meeting** then select **Start an instant meeting**. An instance of meeting will start, this will lead you to the meeting room.

![3-cam.jpg](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43066415732109)

**Step 4**

In the address bar of Google Chrome, click on the camera icon.

![4-cam.jpg](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43066415733133)

**Step 5**

Select _Always Allow https://meet.google.com to Access Your Camera and Microphone_.

![5-cam.jpg](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43066415735693)

**Step 6**

Click **Done**. Your camera and microphone should now be working properly.

![6-cam.jpg](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43066405538189)

[> > \> back to top](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43066343347981-Google-Meet-Troubleshooting-Guide#h_01KG4J2YWK6721SAE1B9YMGDX7)

* * *

## [**Poor Video Quality during Meeting**](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43066343347981-Google-Meet-Troubleshooting-Guide\#h_01KG4PN2W08FKMP0ZDC3TD0Q7V)

**BACKGROUND**

_Several factors may affect the quality of video you see during meetings. For starters, your internet connection might not be stable or strong enough to support the call. It also might be because there are several applications that uses the same resources (i.e., internet bandwidth, memory, video card) that affects the quality of the video._

### What should I do if I am encountering poor video quality during meeting?

If you experience poor video quality on Google Meet, especially when another meeting participant is presenting, follow the steps below to improve your video quality:

1. Check if your internet connection is stable and can support the call.

2. Close other browser tabs or applications that may be using up resources.

3. Make sure that your camera is turned off and your microphone is on mute to reduce the resources Google Meet uses.


[> > \> back to top](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43066343347981-Google-Meet-Troubleshooting-Guide#h_01KG4J2YWK6721SAE1B9YMGDX7)

## FAQ's - Admission Document Requirements – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43158995168269-FAQ-s-Admission-Document-Requirements

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43158995168269-FAQ-s-Admission-Document-Requirements#main-content)

### **❓ FAQs — Physical Document Requirements for Official Admission and Enrollment to MMDC, MMCL**

|     |
| --- |
| **Form 137 vs Form 138**<br>**What is the difference between a Form 138 and Form 137? Do I have to submit both documents even if they have the same content (my high school transcript)?** |
| The **Form 138** or **SF-9 i** s your **high school report card** showing grades from a specific school year or grade level only. What is specifically needed for admission is your Grade 12 or 4th year high school report card. This document is usually printed on various sizes of card stock, which is thicker than most office bond papers.<br>![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43158995166477)![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43158995166605)<br>The **Form 137** or **SF-10** is your **permanent student record** showing a student's academic and personal history throughout high school. This contains a student's personal information, academic records (grades per grading period), attendance record (days present and absent) and a Certificate of Transfer to verify eligibility for the next grade level at the end. This document is usually printed on a long bond paper, back-to-back.<br>![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43158995166989)<br>While the F138 is usually given to the parent/guardian or student personally at the end of every semester, the F137 required for admission to college has to be requested from the school by the student and is released sealed, to be opened by the school Registrar only. _**Both the physical and original copies of your Form 137 and Form 138 are required to be submitted.**_ |

|     |
| --- |
| **Credit Evaluation**<br>**I enrolled at a different college/university before transferring to MMDC, but I only attended one semester and did not finish my program there. I will opt out of course credit evaluation and declare myself as a Freshman since I already have my high school report card with me. Can I just request a Form 137 from my high school and submit them as my admission requirements?** |
| No, you are still considered a transfer student. Please note that your admission requirements depend on your academic history and should follow the proper order of your school admission/transfer timeline. If you were enrolled under a Bachelor’s degree program at the school you last attended before enrolling at MMDC, you need to submit the requirements for transferee students.<br>Additionally, F137 is issued only once and indicated in it is the school where you will be enrolling into next. The F-137 that you will submit to MMCL should have the remarks **"Copy for Mapua Malayan Colleges Laguna."** |

|     |
| --- |
| **I already have my F137/SF10 issued by my previous high school, but it doesn’t have the remarks "Copy for Mapúa Malayan Colleges Laguna.” Can I submit this one instead?** |
| F137/SF10 documents sent to us without the required remarks will be considered invalid and marked as incomplete. You will have to coordinate directly with your previous school to issue you another original revised document to fulfill this admission requirement. If you require an F137 request letter, please refer to [https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/37478613702669-Form-137-Request-Letter](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/37478613702669-Form-137-Request-Letter)<br>![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43158979872525) |

|     |
| --- |
| **I graduated a long time ago and finished high school under the old Basic Education Curriculum (BEC). I did not go through Grades 11 and 12. Do I still need to submit my F138 and F137?** |
| Yes. Please also note the importance of coordinating with your previous high school about the required remarks for your F137. If you require an F137 request letter, please refer to [https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/37478613702669-Form-137-Request-Letter](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/37478613702669-Form-137-Request-Letter) |

|     |
| --- |
| **I seem to have misplaced/damaged my F138/SF9 Report Card. Can I just submit my F137/SF10?** |
| If you find that you have misplaced your F138/SF9 report card or that it had been damaged beyond use, you will have to coordinate with your previous school directly to confirm if they issue a second copy to their students and provide them with a notarized Affidavit of Loss.<br>In the case that they do not issue a second copy of your F138, kindly ask if they can issue you a certificate stating that they acknowledge that your report card was misplaced/damaged but cannot provide a second copy. It is important that you mail this certificate along with your F137 with correct remarks and a copy of your Affidavit of Loss so that the Registrar's Office may waive your F138 in your records and mark your requirements complete. |

|     |
| --- |
| **Where can I get the Certificate of Honorable Dismissal with Transfer Credentials Return Slip?** |
| This document should be included in the Transfer Credentials package you requested from your previous school upon transferring out. However, note that schools differ in their document request policies and processes so it is highly encouraged that you coordinate directly with your previous school for clarification.<br>![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43158979872653) |

|     |
| --- |
| **I was issued a Certificate of Honorable Dismissal, but the document does not have a return slip.** |
| We acknowledge that this is the process for some schools. You will still need to submit your Certificate of Honorable Dismissal to us for processing. We will then issue you a certified true copy (CTC) of your Certificate of Honorable Dismissal attached to a request letter addressed to your previous school so they may release your Official Transcript of Records with the remarks: "Copy for Mapúa Malayan Colleges Laguna." |

|     |
| --- |
| **My previous school instructed me to submit the Return Slip back to them once signed. Please clarify the process.** |
| There are two types of Transcript of Records (TOR) documents: one for evaluation purposes and one with specific remarks to the school you will be transferring to– in your case, MMDC, which is a college under Mapúa Malayan Colleges Laguna.<br>Transfer credentials packages usually only include a TOR for evaluation. In order for your transcript to be issued with the required remarks, you need to first submit your Return Slip to our office where it will be processed for signing by the MMCL Registrar. <br>Once signed, you need to pick up your Return Slip at the MMCL Registrar’s Office and submit it to your previous school so they may release your official Transcript of Records with the remarks: "Copy for Mapúa Malayan Colleges Laguna." |

|     |
| --- |
| **My previous school issued my Transcript of Records with the remarks: “Copy for Mapúa Malayan Digital College.” Will this be accepted?** |
| Unfortunately, your TOR with remarks for MMDC will still be marked invalid. It is necessary that your transcript is addressed to the institution you will be transferring to. Since MMDC is a college under MMCL, the proper remarks would be "Copy for Mapúa Malayan Colleges Laguna." You will be asked to coordinate with your previous school for guidance on how to obtain a corrected version of your TOR. |

|     |
| --- |
| **I am now staying in a city/province far from the last school I attended and I have a busy schedule due to work. Can I submit a Certificate of Good Moral Character from my employer instead?** |
| Only documents issued by your last school attended will be accepted. As enrolling at an institution to further your education requires strong commitment, we encourage making time to process admission document requests from your previous school or arrange for an authorized person to do so on your behalf. |

|     |
| --- |
| **I already graduated and this is my second Bachelor’s degree. What admission requirements do I need to submit?** |
| You will follow the admission requirements for transferee students which include a Certificate of Honorable Dismissal with Transfer Credentials Return Slip and a Transcript of Records with the remarks: "Copy for Mapúa Malayan Colleges Laguna." |

|     |
| --- |
| **I graduated from a diploma/associate degree program. What admission requirements do I need to submit?** |
| You will follow the admission requirements for freshman/high school graduate students which include a F-138/SF-9 Report Card and F-137/SF-10 Learner’s Permanent Record with remarks: “Copy for Mapúa Malayan Colleges Laguna.” |

|     |
| --- |
| **My school has closed/ceased operations after I graduated and I do not have a copy of my transcript/learner’s record. Will my admission requirements be waived?** |
| You will have to go to the Division or Regional Office (DepEd if you are a high school graduate, CHED if you are a transfer student). As all schools are required to submit their records to the Division Office, they should have a copy of your transcript/learner’s record. Kindly request for a certified true copy (CTC) of any of your academic records they have and submit these along with a certification officially confirming the closure of your last attended school.<br>![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43158995167885) |

|     |
| --- |
| **I am an Alternative Learning System (ALS) Accreditation and Equivalency (A&E) High School level passer and my school does not issue an F137 or F138. What requirements do I need to submit?** |
| Kindly submit your ALS Form 5/AF5 Learner's Permanent Record and Certificate of Rating in place of a Form 137 and Form 138. |

## Sign In to the Help Center for Full Access – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43266806512397-Sign-In-to-the-Help-Center-for-Full-Access

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43266806512397-Sign-In-to-the-Help-Center-for-Full-Access#main-content)

## **How to Sign In**

**Signing in allows you to:**

- Access all Help Center content
- View and track your submitted requests
- Open MMDC-only guides


1. Click **Sign In** on the Help Center homepage.

**![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43266806510861)**

2. Enter your **MMDC learner email** and password.
   - If you’ve signed in before, enter your password.
   - If you forgot your password, click **Forgot password?** to reset it.



     ![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43266806511117)
3. If this is your first time signing in, click **Get a password** and follow the instructions sent to your email.
4. You’ll be redirected back to the Help Center homepage once signed in.



![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43266806511373)


To view your submitted tickets, click the dropdown next to your name and select **Requests**.

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/43266832486029)

* * *

## **Use Your MMDC Learner Email**

Always sign in using your **MMDC learner Google account (lr.xxxxx@mmdc.mcl.edu.ph)**.

Documents linked in the Help Center are shared within the MMDC Google environment and may not be accessible using personal email accounts. Signing in with your MMDC account ensures secure, uninterrupted access to all resources.

## Google Drive Troubleshooting Guide – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43289386348301-Google-Drive-Troubleshooting-Guide

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43289386348301-Google-Drive-Troubleshooting-Guide#main-content)

|     |
| --- |
| ## **Overview** |

* * *

## **Table of Contents**

- [Video is not playing in my Google Drive](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43289386348301-Google-Drive-Troubleshooting-Guide#h_01KG4NCJQX36R287VTF3TB53N3)
- [Shared file is crashing or not updating quickly](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43289386348301-Google-Drive-Troubleshooting-Guide#h_01KG4NHAH0ME637XMK0TZBNVN6)

* * *

## **Video is not playing in my Google Drive**

### Background

Google Drive has the capability to play videos uploaded in it. If Google Drive is not able to play videos, it is most likely because of browser or the computer's hardware settings:

**Browser** **Version**: One of the reasons Google Drive cannot play a video is due to its current version. Older versions may not be in sync with the settings needed for the video to play.

**Video** **Format**: Google Drive [supports a handful of video formats](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/17673405039245-Supported-files-and-allowed-file-sizes). The format of the video being played might not be supported by Google Drive.

**Video** **Resolution**: Google Drive supports up to  1920x1080p videos. Any video exceeds the maximum resolution fails to load or play.

**Internet** **Connection**: For Google Drive to play videos, it needs stable and high-speed internet connection. Google Drive fails to play videos on fluctuating or unstable internet connections.

### TROUBLESHOOTING TIPS

1. Check your internet connection.

2. Update your browser.

3. Clear your browsing data.

4. Check the video format. If Google Drive does not support the video format, you may convert the file to a format which Google Drive [supports](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/17673405039245-Supported-files-and-allowed-file-sizes).


[> > \> back to top](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43289386348301-Google-Drive-Troubleshooting-Guide#h_01KG4J2YWK6721SAE1B9YMGDX7)

* * *

## **Shared File is Crashing or not Updating Quickly**

### BACKGROUND

Files shared to several Google users, especially allowing them to update or comment these files, may cause failure to update quickly or for the file to crash every now and then.

### TROUBLESHOOTING TIPS

If several people are updating or commenting on your shared file and it's crashing or not updating quickly, you may try the following tips:

1. If you are collecting feedback, try using Google Forms instead of allowing users to comment on a document or spreadsheet.

2. If you’re making a copy of a document, don’t include resolved comments and suggestions.

3. Delete older information or move data into a new document.

4. Ask viewers to close the document when they aren’t using it.

5. Reduce the number of people with permission to edit the document.


[> > \> back to top](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/43289386348301-Google-Drive-Troubleshooting-Guide#h_01KG4J2YWK6721SAE1B9YMGDX7)

* * *

## MMDC Launches “State of the Working Student” to Elevate Voices of Filipino Working Learners – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/44220956273549-MMDC-Launches-State-of-the-Working-Student-to-Elevate-Voices-of-Filipino-Working-Learners

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/44220956273549-MMDC-Launches-State-of-the-Working-Student-to-Elevate-Voices-of-Filipino-Working-Learners#main-content)

**Mapúa Malayan Digital College (MMDC)** has officially launched the **State of the Working Student (SWS)** initiative — a nationwide effort to better understand and document the lived experiences of Filipino working students.

The initiative forms part of MMDC’s broader **Step Up sa Pangarap** campaign and its support for the celebration of **National Working Students Day**, reinforcing the College’s commitment to recognizing and supporting **learners who balance work and education.**

**Listening to the Realities of Working Students**

Across the Philippines, thousands of students pursue higher education while maintaining employment. Many navigate long work hours, academic deadlines, financial responsibilities, and family commitments — often simultaneously.

Despite their growing presence in the education and workforce landscape, their experiences are not often the focus of conversations. While some data exists on students and employment, the lived realities of working students - their schedules, pressures, motivations, and support systems -- are rarely documented in a comprehensive way.

The **State of the Working Student** initiative seeks to address this gap by gathering nationwide insights through an online survey that explores:

• Academic access and flexibility

• Work conditions and schedules

• Financial realities

• Digital access and study resources

• Well-being and burnout

• Support systems

• Skills development and career readiness

• Identity, motivation, and future aspirations

The findings will be consolidated into the State of the Working Student Report, which MMDC plans to publish and share publicly with schools, employers, policymakers, and key stakeholders.

**Recognizing and Celebrating Working Students**

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/44221321614605)

In line with the observance of **National Working Students Day every March 21**, the initiative also seeks to recognize and celebrate the perseverance of working students. By sharing their realities and stories, the effort highlights both the challenges they navigate and the achievements they earn along the way — helping working students see that their journeys matter and that they are part of a larger community striving toward similar dreams.

**A Foundational Study and Ongoing Commitment**

This initial survey represents the first phase of what MMDC envisions as a continuing national effort. The College intends to update the study regularly to track trends and evolving realities among working learners.

While outcomes depend on collaboration across institutions and sectors, the long-term intention of the initiative is to contribute to:

**• Improved policies and support systems**

**• More understanding and inclusive workplaces**

**• Data-informed programs and partnerships**

**• Stronger advocacy for working students**

**• Greater representation of working students in national conversations**

“This initiative is about listening first,” Rita De Jesus, MMDC's Director for Student Affairs shared. “Before we can improve systems, we need to understand the full picture of what working students are experiencing today.”

**Invitation to Participate**

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/44221213588877)Working students interested in participating may access the survey through this link: [https://forms.gle/tohKAtRJXK4vLYq27](https://forms.gle/tohKAtRJXK4vLYq27)

MMDC invites all working students across the Philippines, even Filipinos working and studying abroad, to participate in the survey.

By sharing their experiences, respondents contribute to a broader effort to ensure that working students’ voices are recognized and included in conversations that shape education and employment systems.

**As a token of appreciation:**

• Each completed response and each successful referral corresponds to one (1) raffle entry

• Ten (10) respondents will receive ₱500 worth of Gift Certificates

• Winners will be announced on March 21 - National Working Students Day

Participation is voluntary, and all responses will be handled in accordance with the Data Privacy Act of 2012 (Republic Act No. 10173). Data will be analyzed and reported only in aggregated form.

## 3.21 Step Up & Go - Move for Working Students — Wherever You Are! – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/44222012162445-3-21-Step-Up-Go-Move-for-Working-Students-Wherever-You-Are

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/44222012162445-3-21-Step-Up-Go-Move-for-Working-Students-Wherever-You-Are#main-content)

![](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/article_attachments/44316505483149)**Not a race. A movement.**

* * *

In celebration of **National Working Students Day on March 21**, MMDC invites everyone to take part in **3-21 Step Up & Go** — a simple run/ walk/ move-anywhere movement that shows support for working students.

Working students balance **school, work, and personal responsibilities** while pursuing their goals. This activity is a collective gesture of recognition and encouragement for their dedication and perseverance.

On **3.21**, we invite you to move in support of them — wherever you are.

# Run/ Walk/ Move From Anywhere!

|     |
| --- |
| Because working students are everywhere, this run, walk or move can happen **anywhere too.**<br>Participants may join from:<br>- Neighborhood streets<br>  <br>- Parks and campuses<br>  <br>- Gyms or running tracks<br>  <br>- Workplaces<br>  <br>- Their own homes |

# How to Join

|     |
| --- |
| **Participation is simple:**<br>1. **Wear BLUE**<br>   <br>2. **Run, walk or move anywhere**<br>   <br>3. **Track your distance or time** using any fitness or step-tracking app<br>   <br>4. **Share your run/ walk/ move online (FB/ IG/ Tiktok)** |
| Use the official hashtags:<br>**#StepUpForWorkingStudents**<br>**#WorkingStudentsDayPH**<br>To make sure we can see and count your run, please:<br>✔ Post publicly with hashtag, or<br>✔ Tag **@mapuamalayandigital, or**<br>✔ Upload your screenshots/ photos here: [https://forms.gle/AyQjis4KQ4k6kFWLA](https://forms.gle/AyQjis4KQ4k6kFWLA) |

* * *

# Community Prizes

**To celebrate the community coming together** in support of working students, participants who share their run or walk using the official hashtags will have the chance to win prizes and recognition.

### **Performance Awards**

- Best 32.1  Run Pace

- Best 32.1 Walk Pace

- Longest Total Distance (Individual) – Run or Walk

- Overall Top Run Finisher – Best 5K / Best 10K

- Overall Top Walk Finisher – Best 5K / Best 10K


### **Solo Awards**

- Best Selfie

- Best Group / Family Photo

- Best Story

- Best Reel


### **Team & Community Awards**

- Best Team / Family / Club – Highest Combined Distance

- Best Team / Family / Club – Highest Combined Movement Time


|     |
| --- |
| Make sure to share  using the hashtags:<br>**#StepUpForWorkingStudents**<br>**#WorkingStudentsDayPH**<br>To make sure we can see and count your run, please:<br>✔ Post publicly with hashtag, or<br>✔ Tag **@mapuamalayandigital, or**<br>✔ Upload your screenshots/ photos here: [https://forms.gle/AyQjis4KQ4k6kFWLA](https://forms.gle/AyQjis4KQ4k6kFWLA) |

# On March 21, Take a Step With Them

Run.

Walk.

Move.

And help make **National Working Students Day** a growing movement that ensures working students are:

**Seen. Heard. Supported.**

**3–21. Step Up & Go!**

## Step Up Your Success: Career Conversations – MMDC

URL: https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/44222730816781-Step-Up-Your-Success-Career-Conversations

[Skip to main content](https://support.mmdc.mcl.edu.ph/hc/en-us/articles/44222730816781-Step-Up-Your-Success-Career-Conversations#main-content)

**Mapúa Malayan Digital College (MMDC)** is launching **Step Up Your Success: Career Conversations** — a digital roadshow designed to help MMDC students strengthen their career readiness and explore opportunities across different industries.

While the campaign aligns with the National Working Students Day, **Step Up Your Success: Career Conversations is open to ALL MMDC STUDENTS** who want to build the skills, knowledge, and connections needed to succeed in today’s evolving workforce.

Following the **Nationwide Run for Working Students on March 21**, MMDC will begin hosting a series of online sessions where students can learn from career mentors, industry practitioners, and employer partners who are committed to supporting the next generation of professionals.

Through these conversations, students will gain practical career insights, develop essential professional skills, and explore pathways across different industries.

### **Two Career-Focused Learning Tracks**

The Digital Roadshow will feature sessions under **two key themes**, each designed to help students prepare for meaningful and sustainable careers.

1. ### Career Readiness & Career Preparation


These sessions will focus on practical skills that help students confidently transition from college to the professional world.

Students will learn how to present their experiences, communicate effectively in professional environments, and strategically plan their career paths.

Session topics include:

- **Step Up Your Resume**

How to highlight your academic projects, internships, and work experience effectively.

- **Step Up Your Interview Skills**

Practical strategies to communicate your strengths and experiences with confidence.

- **Step Up Your Professional Communication**

Developing clear, effective communication skills for the workplace.

- **Step Up Your Career Strategy**

How to plan your career path and identify growth opportunities early.

- **Step Up Your Digital Presence**

Building a professional online identity and maximizing platforms such as LinkedIn.


These sessions feature **career coaches, menotrs, professionals, and industry practitioners** who will share insights based on real workplace experiences.

2. ### Industry & Employer Conversations


The second track of the roadshow will bring students closer to **industry leaders and MMDC employer partners** who will share insights about careers across different sectors.

These conversations will help students better understand:

• emerging industry trends

• the skills employers are looking for in graduates

• career pathways in different industries

• how students can prepare for future opportunities

Industry conversations include topics such as:

- **Step Up to Careers in Technology and Digital Innovation**

Exploring opportunities in software development, data, and digital transformation.

- **Step Up to Business and Operations Careers**

Career pathways in project management, business analytics, and operations leadership.

- **Step Up to Digital Marketing and Creative Industries**

Insights into careers in digital marketing, branding, and creative production.

- **Step Up to Customer Experience and Service Leadership**

Opportunities in service industries, operations management, and leadership development.


These sessions feature **industry professionals and employer partners from technology companies, digital organizations, business services firms, and other growing sectors.**

* * *

### **Upcoming Sessions**

The Digital Roadshow will officially begin **after the Nationwide Run for Working Students on March 21.**

The **full calendar of sessions and invitations to individual talks will be released soon**, and students will be able to register for the sessions that best match their interests and career goals.

Stay tuned for announcements through MMDC’s official channels.
